## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics
**Analysis**: The task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, which falls within classical mechanics and nonlinear dynamics. The acceleration dv/dt is typically expressed as a function of displacement x (restoring force), velocity v (damping), and time t (external or parametric driving), capturing complex oscillatory behaviors such as limit cycles, frequency shifts, and chaotic motion.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple harmonic motion with constant stiffness)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic stiffness for hardening or softening spring)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (1 - c1 * x**2) * v + c2 * x (nonlinear damping producing limit cycles)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 + c2 * x (velocity-dependent nonlinear damping)
- Forced linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (harmonic driving with linear damping)
- Forced Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (cubic stiffness with periodic forcing)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x (time-dependent stiffness modulation)
- Pendulum equation: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force for finite amplitude)
- Softening spring model: dv_dt = c0 * x / (1 + c1 * x**2) (saturating restoring force)
- Quadratic damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * abs(v) (drag proportional to square of velocity)
- Toda oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * x) + c2 (exponential interaction potential)
- Cubic-quintic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order stiffness corrections)
- Asymmetric restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (parity-breaking potential)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ‚Üí Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ‚Üí Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ‚Üí Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ‚Üí Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ‚Üí Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Even-order restoring force ‚Üí x**2 term indicates asymmetric potential
- Cubic restoring force ‚Üí x**3 term causes amplitude-dependent frequency (hardening/softening)
- Nonlinear damping saturation ‚Üí v/(1+abs(v)) or sigmoidal functions for bounded damping force
- Limit cycle behavior ‚Üí negative linear damping combined with positive higher-order damping (e.g., c0*v - c1*v**3)
- Parametric resonance ‚Üí product of displacement x and a time-periodic coefficient (e.g., cos(c*t)*x)
- Hardening vs softening spring ‚Üí sign of cubic term c1: positive for hardening (frequency increases with amplitude), negative for softening
- Quadratic drag ‚Üí term v*abs(v) or v**2 proportional to v^2, typical for fluid damping at high speeds
- Exponential restoring force ‚Üí exp(c1*x) indicates Toda-like potentials with soliton dynamics
